The Form of a Judge's Judgment: Does 'Thabata 'Indi' Suffice?
Ruling on when a judge passes judgment based on witnesses in a case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a judge's statement 'thabata 'indi' and distinguish it from the requirement of explicit pronouncement.

Core Idea
A judge's clear determination suffices; explicit words like 'I judge' are not required in the Hanafi school.

When a judge hears a case and witnesses testify, he must issue a judgment. But what words must he use? Is it necessary to say 'I judge' or 'I decide'? In this lesson, we examine a key dispute within the Hanafi school: whether the expression 'thabata 'indi' (it has been established before me) constitutes a binding judgment, or whether more explicit language is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The question is what form of words makes a judge's ruling valid. The base text states he 'passes judgment', but does not specify the wording.
2
Locate the two Hanafi positions
Abu 'Asim al-'Amiri and others hold that 'thabata 'indi' is sufficient; Mahmud al-Uzjandi requires 'hukmtu' or 'qadaytu'.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyse the reasoning for each position
The first position emphasizes the judge's substantive determination; the second emphasizes formality and clarity.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in later fatwa works (al-Fatawa al-'Alamgiriyyah) is that 'thabata 'indi' suffices.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.
5
Apply the ruling
If a judge in a modern court says 'It is proven to me that...', that constitutes a valid judgment in Hanafi law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي ثمَّ شَرَعَ بعد ذلك فيما يفعلُهُ القاضي إذا كان الخصم حاضراً، أو لم يكن، فقال: (فإن شهدوا على خصم حاضر حكم بها). قوله: حكم بها؛ قال مشايخنا: ينبغي للقاضي إذا أراد الحكم أن يقول للخصمين: احكم بينكما، وهذا على وجه الاحتياط، حتى أنه إذا كان في التقليد خلل يصير حكماً بتحكيمهما. وإذا قال القاضي: ثبت عندي أن لهذا على هذا كذا، هل يكون هذا حكماً عن القاضي؟ (1) كان القاضي الإمام أبو عاصم العامري يفتي بأنه حكم، وهو اختيار شمس الأئمة الحلواني له، واختيار الصدر الشهيد له، وفي «الخانية»: وعليه الفتوى. (2) وكان القاضي شمس الإسلام محمود الأوزجنْدِي يقول: لا بد أن يقول القاضي: قضيت، أو يقول: حكمت، أو أنفذت عليك القضاء، وهكذا ذكره الناطفي في «واقعاته». والصحيح أن قوله: حكمت وقضيتُ ليس بشرط، وأن قوله: ثبت عندي يكفي، وكذلك إذا قال: ظهر عندي، أو قال: علمت، فهذا كله حكم. هذا ملتقط ما في «الفتاوى العالمكيرية».
Chapter on the Judge's Writing to Another Judge. Then he began after that with what the judge does if the opponent is present or not, so he said: (If they testify against a present opponent, he passes judgment on it.) His saying: He passes judgment on it; Our shaykhs said: The judge, when he wants to pass judgment, should say to the two litigants: 'Arbitrate between yourselves,' and this is out of caution, so that if there is a defect in the appointment, it becomes a judgment by their arbitration. And if the judge says: 'It has been established before me that this one has such-and-such against this one,' is this a judgment from the judge? (1) The judge Imam Abu 'Asim al-'Amiri used to give fatwa that it is a judgment, and this is the choice of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani for him, and the choice of al-Sadr al-Shahid for him, and in al-Khaniyyah: And upon it is the fatwa. (2) And the judge Shams al-Islam Mahmud al-Uzjandi used to say: The judge must say: 'I have decided,' or say: 'I have judged,' or 'I have enforced the judgment upon you,' and thus al-Natifi mentioned it in his Waqi'at. And the correct is that his saying 'I have judged' and 'I have decided' is not a condition, and that his saying 'It has been established before me' suffices, and likewise if he says 'It has appeared to me' or says 'I know,' all of this is a judgment. This is compiled from al-Fatawa al-'Alamgiriyyah.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the section on a judge writing to another judge, concerning the form of a valid judgment. The base matn says: 'If witnesses testify against a present opponent, he passes judgment on it.' The commentator then discusses the proper formulation of a judgment. He begins by noting that some scholars recommend the judge tell the litigants to arbitrate, as a precaution in case the judge's own appointment was defective. The core dispute is whether a judge's statement 'it has been established before me' (thabata 'indi) constitutes a binding judgment. Imam Abu 'Asim al-'Amiri, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, and al-Sadr al-Shahid all held that it does, and this is the view upon which fatwa is given according to al-Khaniyyah. In contrast, Shams al-Islam Mahmud al-Uzjandi insisted that the judge must explicitly say 'I have judged' or 'I have decided.' The correct and relied-upon position in the later Fatawa 'Alamgiriyyah is that explicit words like 'hukmtu' or 'qadaytu' are not a condition; rather, 'thabata 'indi' (it has been established before me) or similar expressions like 'it appeared to me' or 'I know' are sufficient to constitute a judgment. This reflects the Hanafi principle that the essence of judgment is the judge's determination, not the specific wording.

Key Terms
ثبت عندي (thabata 'indi): A statement by the judge indicating that the evidence has established the claim in his view.
حكم بها (hakama biha): He passes judgment based on that testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in al-Fatawa al-'Alamgiriyyah, which utterance by a judge constitutes a valid judgment?
A) Only 'I have judged' (حكمت)
B) Only 'I have decided' (قضيت)
C) 'It has been established before me' (ثبت عندي)
D) Neither A nor B nor C

Key Takeaway
A judge's clear statement 'thabata 'indi' constitutes a valid judgment in the Hanafi school; explicit words like 'hukmtu' are not required.

Judge's Wording for a Valid Judgment
Intra-Hanafi dispute on judge's wording

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on the sufficiency of 'thabata 'indi' for a judge's ruling and distinguish it from the view requiring explicit wording.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling is valid with 'thabata 'indi' – explicit words are not required.

The judge's pronouncement of judgment is a key moment in litigation. Does it require a specific verbal formula? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: whether saying 'it is established to me' (thabata 'indi) is enough, or whether the judge must explicitly say 'I have adjudged' (qadaitu) or 'I have judged' (hakamtu). The relied-upon position is clear and practical.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The passage addresses what wording from the judge constitutes a valid judicial ruling (hukm). Is there a required verbal formula?
2
Locate the two positions
Find the first position: Abu 'Asim al-'Amiri, al-Halwani, and al-Sadr al-Shahid accept 'thabata 'indi' as a valid judgment. The second position: al-Uzjandi and al-Natafi require explicit 'qadaitu' or 'hakamtu'.
Both are Hanafi scholars, so this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Determine the relied-upon view
The text declares the correct view (as-sahih) that explicit words are not a condition; 'thabata 'indi', 'zahara 'indi', and 'alimtu' all constitute a valid judgment. This is the mufta bihi from al-Fatawa al-'Alamgiriyya.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a judge says 'thabata 'indi', according to the first view the ruling is complete; according to the second view it would not be considered a valid judgment until he says 'qadaitu'.
This affects the enforceability of the ruling.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a case where the judge listens to witnesses, then says 'It has become clear to me that the defendant owes 100 dirhams'. Ask: is this a valid judgment? Under the relied-upon view, yes.
The judge must still follow proper procedure, but the wording is flexible.

Source Text

فصل في كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي
فإن شهدوا على خصم حاضر حكم بها
ثُمَّ شَرَعَ بعد ذلك فيما يفعلُهُ القاضي إذا كان الخصم حاضراً، أو لم يكن ، فقال : (فإن شهدوا على خصم حاضر حكم بها".
باقتراض ، قال في «البزازية ) : لو وجد المديون من يقرضه فلم يفعل فهو ظالم. وفي (كراهية) «القُنْية»: لو كان للمديون حرفةٌ تفضي إلى قضاء دينه فامتنع منها لا يعذر. انتهى. أو يتقاضى غريمه بأن كان له مالٌ على غريم موسر. كما صرح به في «البزازيّة» (۳) ، وإنّما قال بضدّه ولم يقل بغنائه ؛ لأنّ المتبادر من الغناء هو ملك النصاب، ويحبس في ما دونه. كما صرح به في «الفتح»"، وغيره. Chapter on the Judge's Letter to Another Judge. If they (witnesses) testify against a present defendant, he (the judge) pronounces judgment upon it. Then he (the author) began after that with what the judge does when the defendant is present or not, and said: 'If they testify against a present defendant, he pronounces judgment upon it.' By borrowing, it is stated in al-Bazzaziyya: If a debtor finds someone who would lend to him but does not do so, he is an oppressor. And in Karahiyya of al-Qunya: If the debtor has a profession that would lead to paying his debt and he abstains from it, he is not excused. End. Or he demands payment from his creditor if he has money owed by a solvent creditor, as stated in al-Bazzaziyya. He said 'its opposite' and did not say 'solvency' because the immediate understanding of solvency is ownership of the nisab, and imprisonment is for less than that, as stated in al-Fath and others. [1] His statement: 'he pronounces judgment upon it'; our scholars said: It is appropriate for the judge, when he wants to judge, to say to the two litigants: 'Judge between yourselves,' and this is by way of precaution, so that if there is a defect in the delegation, it becomes a judgment by their arbitration. And if the judge says: 'It is established to me that this one has such-and-such against this one,' is this a judgment from the judge? Judge Abu 'Asim al-'Amiri used to give fatwa that it is a judgment, and it is the choice of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, and the choice of al-Sadr al-Shahid, and in al-Khaniyya: upon it is the fatwa. And Judge Shams al-Islam Mahmud al-Uzjandi used to say: It is necessary for the judge to say 'I have adjudged' or 'I have judged' or 'I have enforced judgment upon you,' and al-Natafi mentioned this in his Waqi'at. And the correct view is that his saying 'I have judged' and 'I have adjudged' is not a condition, and that his saying 'it is established to me' suffices, and likewise if he says 'it has appeared to me' or 'I have known,' all of this is a judgment. This is extracted from al-Fatawa al-'Alamgiriyya.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with commentary on the judge's action when witnesses testify in the presence of the defendant. It begins with the chapter heading on inter-judge correspondence. The matn states that if witnesses testify against a present defendant, the judge pronounces judgment. The commentary then digresses to discuss the situation of a debtor who can borrow but refuses, or who has a profession but avoids it, citing al-Bazzaziyya and al-Qunya. These are considered oppressive or inexcusable. The passage then returns to the main topic: the judge's recommended procedure is to ask the litigants to appoint him as arbitrator as a precaution. The core issue discussed is the wording of the judgment. Two positions within the Hanafi school are presented: one, held by Judge Abu 'Asim al-'Amiri, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, and al-Sadr al-Shahid, is that saying 'it is established to me' (thabata 'indi) is sufficient for a valid judgment. The other, held by Judge Shams al-Islam Mahmud al-Uzjandi and al-Natafi, requires explicit words like 'I have adjudged' (qadaitu) or 'I have judged' (hakamtu). The text declares the correct view to be that explicit words are not a condition; 'thabata 'indi', 'zahara 'indi', or 'alimtu' all constitute a valid judgment, citing al-Fatawa al-'Alamgiriyya. This is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
حكم بها (hukma biha): The judge pronounces judgment based on the testimony.
ثبت عندي (thabata 'indi): It is established to me; a phrase considered sufficient for a valid judgment if said by the judge.
قضيت (qadaitu): I have adjudged; a phrase some Hanafi scholars require for a valid judgment, but not the relied-upon view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, which of the following phrases, if said by a judge, constitutes a valid judgment?
A) I have adjudged (qadaitu)
B) It is established to me (thabata 'indi)
C) Both A and B are valid
D) Only A is valid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a judge's ruling is valid by any clear expression of his decision, such as 'thabata 'indi', without needing specific verbal formulas like 'qadaitu'.

Judgment on an Absent Defendant and the Sijill
Ruling on absent defendant and definition of sijill

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on judgment against an absent defendant, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the definition of absence, and explain the nature and purpose of the sijill.

Core Idea
Judgment on an absent defendant is restricted; the sijill is the record, not the judgment itself.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya discusses two procedural aspects of qada: the recording of judgments in the sijill and the conditions under which a judge may rule against an absent defendant. The first clarifies that the judge is not obligated to write the judgment but may do so for preservation. The second reveals an important intra-Hanafi difference: while the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) requires the defendant to be at travel distance, the fatwa adopts Abu Yusuf's view, allowing judgment if the defendant cannot return within a day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage addresses two distinct topics: (a) the writing of the judgment (sijill) and (b) the conditions for ruling against an absent defendant (gha'ib).
These appear in separate sections of the text.
2
Analyze the sijill ruling
Determine that writing the judgment is not obligatory on the judge; it is a precautionary measure. The plaintiff bears the cost of the writing material unless the treasury has funds.
The judge's direct duty is to pronounce judgment, not to record it.
3
State the default rule on absent defendant
The default rule is that a judge does not pronounce judgment against a defendant who is absent (gha'ib). An exception exists under certain conditions.
The text says 'if they testify against an absent defendant, he does not pronounce judgment.'
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on the condition
In zahir al-riwayah, the condition is that the absent defendant be at travel distance (masirat al-safar). Abu Yusuf holds that it suffices if the defendant cannot return within the same day. The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view.
This is a key ikhtilaf within the school; the mufta bihi is the more lenient position.
5
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a defendant in a nearby town (e.g., 30 km away), determine whether judgment can be passed in his absence under the mufta bihi.
Consider the defendant's ability to return within the day based on transportation and court hours.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكتب به، وهو السجل، وإن شهدوا على غائب لم يحكم
[١]قوله : وكتب ؛ القاضي به ؛ أي ما يحكم ؛ لئلا ينسى الواقعة على طول الزمان، وليكون الكاتب ذاكراً لها وإلا فلا يحتاج إلى كتابة الحكم ؛ لأنه قد تم بحضور الخصم بنفسه، أو من يقوم مقامه.
وهذه الكتابة ليست بواجبة على القاضي، وإنما الواجب عليه مباشرة القضاء، وهذه الصحيفة التي يكتب عليها يكلف الطالب ليأتي بها ؛ لأنَّ منفعة ذلك له، ولو أمر القاضي بها من مال بيت المال ، إن كان فيه سعة فلا بأس به. كما هو مصرّح. [٢] قوله : وهو السجل ؛ الحكمي ؛ لأنه سجله : أي أحكمه، وتحقيق السجلّ مرَّ سابقاً، قال في «البحر») : السجل : الحجَّةُ التي فيها حكم القاضي، ولكن هذا في عرفهم، وفي عرفنا : السجل كتاب كبير يضبط فيه وقائع الناس، وما يحكم القاضي، وما يكتب عليه.
[٣] قوله : على غائب ؛ كان في محلة أخرى، أو قرية، أو بلدة، ويشترط في ظاهر الرواية مسيرة السفر، وعن أبي يوسف الله : يجوز فيما لا يرجع في يومه، وفي «السراجية»: وعليه الفتوى.
[٤] قوله : لم يحكم ؛ وإن الحكم على الغائب لا يجوز ؛ لِمَا عرف في موضعه، ولو حكم به حاكم يرى ذلك ، ثمَّ نقل إليه نفذه بخلاف الكتاب الحكمي حيث لا ينفذ خلاف مذهبه ؛ لأنَّ الأول محكوم به فلزمه، والثاني ابتداء حكم، فلا يجوز له، ذكره العلامةُ الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في شرح الكنز )) . وقال في «البحر»(۳) : هذا يدلُّ على أنَّ الحاكم على الغائب إذا كان حنفيّاً، فإنّ...
And he writes it, and it is the sijill. And if they testify against an absent defendant, he does not pronounce judgment. [1] His statement: 'And he writes'; the judge writes it, i.e., what he judges, lest he forget the incident over time, and so that the writer remembers it. Otherwise, writing the judgment is not needed because it has been completed by the presence of the defendant himself or his representative. This writing is not obligatory upon the judge; rather, what is obligatory upon him is the direct performance of judgment. The plaintiff is required to bring the sheet on which he writes because the benefit is for him. If the judge orders it from the treasury, if there is capacity, there is no harm. As stated explicitly. [2] His statement: 'and it is the sijill'; the judicial record; because he recorded it, i.e., he perfected it. The definition of sijill has passed previously. It is said in al-Bahr: The sijill is the document containing the judge's ruling, but this is in their custom. In our custom, the sijill is a large book in which the incidents of people and what the judge rules and what is written are recorded. [3] His statement: 'against an absent defendant'; he is in another district, village, or town. In the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), the condition is the distance of travel. From Abu Yusuf: It is permitted for what cannot be returned within the same day. In al-Sirajiyya: Upon it is the fatwa. [4] His statement: 'he does not pronounce judgment'; and that judgment on an absent defendant is not permissible, as is known in its place. If a judge who holds that view rules, then the case is transferred to another judge, he enforces it, contrary to the judicial letter (kitab hukmi) where it is not enforced contrary to his school, because the first is already ruled upon and thus binding, while the second is a new judgment, so it is not permissible for him. Al-Zayla'i mentioned this in Sharh al-Kanz. And it is said in al-Bahr: This indicates that if the judge ruling on the absent defendant is a Hanafi, then...
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with commentary on two issues: the writing of the judgment (sijill) and the prohibition of judgment against an absent defendant. The matn states that the judge writes the judgment (the sijill) and that if witnesses testify against an absent defendant, he does not pronounce judgment. The commentary explains that writing the judgment is not obligatory on the judge; it is a precaution to avoid forgetting. The plaintiff is responsible for providing the writing material. The sijill is defined as the document containing the judge's ruling, or in later custom, a large record book. For an absent defendant, the condition for valid judgment is that the defendant must be at a travel distance (zahir al-riwayah). Abu Yusuf allows judgment if the defendant cannot return within a day, and this is the relied-upon position (fatwa). Judgment on an absent defendant is generally not permissible. However, if a judge who follows a different school rules on an absent defendant and the case is transferred to another judge, the latter enforces it because it is a previous binding ruling, unlike a judicial letter that would not be enforced if it contradicts the enforcing judge's school. The text references al-Zayla'i in Sharh al-Kanz and al-Bahr.

Key Terms
السجل (al-sijill): The document containing the judge's ruling; in later custom, a large record book for court proceedings.
غائب (gha'ib): A defendant who is not present in court and is at a distance meeting the travel condition or, per Abu Yusuf, cannot return within the day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (fatwa) in the Hanafi school, when is a judge permitted to rule against an absent defendant?
A) Only if the defendant is at travel distance (three days journey)
B) If the defendant cannot return to court within the same day
C) Always, as long as the judge has proof
D) Never, judgment on an absent person is invalid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits judgment on an absent defendant only when the defendant is at a distance that prevents return within a day, and the sijill is the record of judgment, not the judgment itself.

Writing the Record and Judging the Absent Party in Hanafi Qada
Explaining the record of judgment and conditions for judging an absent defendant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on writing the judgment record and explain the Hanafi position on judging an absent defendant, including the condition of travel distance and the enforcement of cross-madhhab judgments.

Core Idea
Writing the record is recommended, not obligatory; judging an absent defendant is invalid without the condition of travel distance.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains two important procedural issues in Hanafi qada: the judge's record (al-sijill) and the permissibility of issuing a judgment against an absent defendant. While the record is merely a tool to prevent forgetfulness, the ruling on the absent party involves a nuanced position: generally prohibited in the apparent narration, but subject to an intra-madhhab difference and a cross-madhhab consideration. Understanding these rules is essential for a judge or mufti to ensure valid judicial proceedings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on writing the judgment record
Determine whether writing the judgment is obligatory or merely recommended. The text states it is not obligatory (laysat bi wajibah) but is done to avoid forgetfulness.
The judge's direct duty is to judge; writing is auxiliary.
2
Determine who bears the cost of the record
The plaintiff must bring the paper for writing because the benefit is for him. However, if the public treasury can afford it, it may be used.
3
State the Hanafi ruling on judging an absent party
According to the apparent narration, it is not permissible to judge an absent defendant unless the defendant is at travel distance (masirat al-safar).
The condition of travel distance is a key requirement.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Yusuf allows judgment if the absent person does not return within the same day. The relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi) is the apparent narration requiring travel distance.
Al-Sirajiyyah confirms the fatwa is on the apparent narration.
5
Apply the cross-madhhab enforcement rule
If a Shafi'i judge issues a judgment on an absent defendant, a Hanafi judge must enforce it because it is a final judgment. This differs from a judge's letter (kitab hukmi) which is not binding across madhhabs.
The key distinction: final judgment vs. initial judgment.

وكتب به، وهو السجل، وإن شهدوا على غائب لم يحكم
[١]قوله : وكتب به القاضي أي ما يحكم؛ لئلا ينسى الواقعة على طول الزمان، وليكون الكاتب ذاكراً لها وإلا فلا يحتاج إلى كتابة الحكم؛ لأنه قد تم بحضور الخصم بنفسه، أو من يقوم مقامه. وهذه الكتابة ليست بواجبة على القاضي، وإنما الواجب عليه مباشرة القضاء، وهذه الصحيفة التي يكتب عليها يكلف الطالب ليأتي بها؛ لأن منفعة ذلك له، ولو أمر القاضي بها من مال بيت المال، إن كان فيه سعة فلا بأس به. كما هو مصرّح. [٢] قوله : وهو السجل؛ الحكمي؛ لأنه سجله: أي أحكمه، وتحقيق السجلّ مرَّ سابقاً، قال في «البحر»: السجل: الحجة التي فيها حكم القاضي، ولكن هذا في عرفهم، وفي عرفنا: السجل كتاب كبير يضبط فيه وقائع الناس، وما يحكم القاضي، وما يكتب عليه.
[٣] قوله : على غائب؛ كان في محلة أخرى، أو قرية، أو بلدة، ويشترط في ظاهر الرواية مسيرة السفر، وعن أبي يوسف الله: يجوز فيما لا يرجع في يومه، وفي «السراجية»: وعليه الفتوى.
[٤] قوله : لم يحكم؛ وإن الحكم على الغائب لا يجوز؛ لما عرف في موضعه، ولو حكم به حاكم يرى ذلك، ثم نقل إليه نفذه بخلاف الكتاب الحكمي حيث لا ينفذ خلاف مذهبه؛ لأن الأول محكوم به فلزمه، والثاني ابتداء حكم، فلا يجوز له، ذكره العلامة الزيلعي في شرح الكنز. وقال في «البحر»: هذا يدل على أن الحاكم على الغائب إذا كان حنفياً، فإنّ حكمه لا ينفذ لقوله: يرى ذلك، وهو مقيد؛ لأن معنى قولهم: إن القضاء على الغائب ينفذ في أظهر الروايتين؛ إذا كان القاضي شافعياً. انتهى.
And he wrote it, and it is the record. And if they testify against an absent person, he did not judge. [1] His statement: And the judge wrote with it, i.e., what he judged, so that he does not forget the incident over time, and so that the writer remembers it. Otherwise, there is no need to write the judgment because it has been completed in the presence of the litigant himself or his representative. This writing is not obligatory upon the judge; rather, what is obligatory is to undertake the judiciary directly. And this sheet on which he writes is demanded from the plaintiff to bring it because the benefit is for him. If the judge orders it from the public treasury, if there is capacity, there is no harm, as is explicitly stated. [2] His statement: And it is the record; the judgmental, because he recorded it, i.e., he perfected it. The verification of 'record' has passed earlier. He said in 'Al-Bahr': The record is the proof document that contains the judge's judgment, but this is in their custom. In our custom, the record is a large book in which the incidents of people and what the judge judges are recorded. [3] His statement: Against an absent person, if he was in another locality, village, or town. According to the apparent narration, a travel distance is required. From Abu Yusuf: It is permissible if he does not return within the same day. In 'Al-Sirajiyyah': And upon it is the fatwa. [4] His statement: He did not judge. And indeed, judging the absent person is not permissible, as is known in its place. If a judge who holds that view judges, then the case is transferred to him, he implements it, unlike the judgmental letter where he does not implement contrary to his madhhab because the first is a judgment that has been passed so it is binding upon him, and the second is an initial judgment, so it is not permissible for him. This was mentioned by Allamah al-Zaylai in Sharh al-Kanz. And he said in 'Al-Bahr': This indicates that the judge on the absent person, if he is Hanafi, his judgment is not implemented because he says 'he holds that view', and it is restricted because the meaning of their statement: 'Judgment on the absent person is implemented in the more apparent of the two narrations' is when the judge is Shafi'i. End.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling regarding the judge's record (السجل) and the permissibility of judging an absent defendant (الغائب). The base text states that the judge writes his judgment (وكتب به) and that is called السجل. The commentary clarifies that writing the judgment is not obligatory; it is only recommended to prevent forgetfulness. The judge may require the plaintiff to bring the paper for writing, but if the public treasury can afford it, the judge may pay for it. Then the text discusses that if witnesses testify against an absent person, the judge should not issue a judgment (لم يحكم) because the defendant is not present. However, there is an intra-Hanafi difference: in the apparent narration (ظاهر الرواية), the absent party must be at a travel distance (مسيرة السفر), while according to Abu Yusuf, it is permissible if the absent party does not return within the same day. The relied-upon fatwa is that of the apparent narration. If a judge who holds the view that it is permissible (e.g., a Shafi'i judge) issues a judgment on an absent person, and then a Hanafi judge is asked to enforce it, the Hanafi judge must enforce it because it is a final judgment, unlike a judge's letter (الكتاب الحكمي) which is an initial judgment not binding on a judge of a different madhhab. This shows that the Hanafi ruling is that judging an absent person is not permissible, but if a Shafi'i judge does so, it is enforceable in the more apparent narration.

Key Terms
السجل (al-sijill): The record or document containing the judge's written judgment.
الغائب (al-gha'ib): A defendant who is not present in the court at the time of testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration (ظاهر الرواية), what condition is required for a judgment to be issued against an absent defendant?
A) The absent party must not return within the same day.
B) The absent party must be at a travel distance (مسيرة السفر).
C) The absent party must have been notified in writing.
D) The judge must be a Shafi'i.

Key Takeaway
Judging an absent defendant is invalid in Hanafi law unless he is at travel distance; any judgment issued by a Hanafi judge without that condition is not enforceable, but final judgments from other madhhaps are respected.

The Judgement Letter (الكتاب الحكمي): Ruling, Conditions, and Istihsan Justification
Explaining the judgmental letter (الكتاب الحكمي) and istihsan justification for accepting it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the judge's letter, state its four conditions, and distinguish it from the record (السجل).

Core Idea
A judge's letter transmitting testimony is accepted by istihsan, not qiyas, to protect rights when in-person attendance is impossible.

This passage clarifies a crucial procedure in Islamic judiciary: a judge writes testimony to another judge. Despite the risk of forgery, the Hanafi school permits it by istihsan, analogizing it to testimony upon testimony. You will learn when it applies, its conditions, and how it differs from a final judgment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept (كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي)
Understand what the 'judgement letter' is: a letter containing testimony from one judge to another for the receiving judge to issue a judgment. It is also called الكتاب الحكمي.
It is real transmission of testimony (نقل الشهادة حقيقة), not a judgment.
2
Distinguish from السجل (the record)
The letter is not a final judgment. The receiving judge may judge according to his own opinion, even if it differs from the writing judge. In contrast, the record (السجل) is a binding judgment that cannot be opposed.
If the receiving judge disagrees, he may not accept the letter.
3
List the four certainty conditions
The letter must be from a known judge to a known judge, regarding a known claim, by a known plaintiff, against a known defendant. All four are explicitly required.
The term 'معلوم' appears four times in the text.
4
Understand the qiyas objection
Strict analogy (qiyas) would prohibit acceptance because: (1) if the writing judge testified orally, it would not be accepted; (2) risk of forgery (handwriting/seal can be imitated).
This is the argument that istihsan overrides.
5
Apply istihsan and the analogy to testimony upon testimony
The scholars permitted it by istihsan due to people's need—a plaintiff may be unable to gather witnesses and opponent in one location. It is analogous to testimony upon testimony (الشهادة على الشهادة), which is also an exception to qiyas for reviving rights.
Istihsan is a valid source in Hanafi methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القضاء / الحبس وكتاب القاضي إلى القاضي

وكتب بالشهادة ليحكم المكتوب إليه بها، وهو الكتاب الحكمي، وكتاب القاضي إلى القاضي، وهو نقل الشهادة حقيقة، ويقبل فيما لا يسقط بشبهة

[١]قوله : وكتب القاضي بالشهادة إلى قاض يكون الخصم في ولايته؛ ليحكم القاضي المكتوب إليه على وجه الخصم؛ لئلا يكون قضاء على الغائب بها؛ أي بهذه الشهادة على رأيه، وإن كان مخالفاً لرأي القاضي الكاتب بخلاف السجل، فإنّه ليس له أن يخالفه، وينقض حكمه؛ لأن السجل محكوم به دون الكتاب؛ ولذا له أن لا يقبل الكتاب دون السجل. كذا في «البحر» نقلا عن «منية المفتي». [٢] قوله : وهو؛ أي ما كتب القاضي فيه الشهادة؛ ليحكم المكتوب إليه بها الكتاب الحكمي المنسوب إلى الحكم باعتبار ما يؤول إليه، أو كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي. ووجه التسمية به ظاهر، وهو نقل الشهادة حقيقة؛ لأن الكاتب لم يحكم بها، وإنما نقلها للمكتوب إليه ليحكم بها؛ ولهذا يحكم المكتوب إليه برأيه، وإن خالف رأيه رأي الكاتب بخلاف السجل كما مر آنفاً.
ويشترط في الكتاب على أن يكون من معلوم إلى معلوم، في مدعى به معلوم لمدع معلوم على مدعى عليه معلوم، والقياس يأبى جواز العمل بكتاب القاضي إلى القاضي؛ لأن القاضي الكاتب لو حضر بنفسه مجلس المكتوب إليه وخبره بلسانه عما في الكتاب لا يعمل به القاضي، فكيف بالكتاب. وفيه شبهة التزوير، إذ الخط يشبه الخط، والخاتم يشبه الخاتم، إلا أنه جوّز استحساناً؛ لحاجة الناس إليه، فإن المدعي قد يتعذر عليه الجمع بين شهوده وخصمه، فأشبه الشهادة على الشهادة، فكما جوز الشهادة على الشهادة؛ لإحياء حقوق العباد
Book of Judiciary / Imprisonment and Book of Judge to Judge. And he wrote with the testimony so that the one written to may judge by it, and it is the judgmental letter, and the book of a judge to a judge, and it is the transmission of testimony in reality, and it is accepted in what is not nullified by suspicion. [1] His statement: And the judge wrote the testimony to a judge in whose jurisdiction the litigant is, so that the judge written to may judge against the litigant, so that there not be a judgment on the absent person by it, i.e., by this testimony according to his opinion, even if it differs from the opinion of the writing judge, unlike the record, for he does not have the right to oppose it and annul his judgment, because the record is a judgment that has been passed, unlike the letter. Hence he may not accept the letter unlike the record. Thus in 'Al-Bahr' quoting from 'Munyat al-Mufti'. [2] His statement: And it is, i.e., what the judge wrote the testimony in, so that the one written to may judge by it, the judgmental letter attributed to judgment in consideration of what it leads to, or the book of a judge to a judge. The reason for the naming is apparent, and it is the transmission of testimony in reality because the writer did not judge by it, but rather transmitted it to the one written to so that he may judge by it. Hence the one written to judges according to his own opinion, even if his opinion differs from that of the writing judge, unlike the record as mentioned previously. Conditions are required for the letter: it must be from a known judge to a known judge, concerning a known claim, by a known plaintiff, against a known defendant. And analogy (qiyas) would prevent the permissibility of acting upon a judge's letter to a judge, because if the writing judge himself attended the court of the one written to and informed him verbally of what is in the letter, the judge would not act upon it, so how much less the letter? And there is the suspicion of forgery, as handwriting resembles handwriting and the seal resembles the seal. However, it is permitted by istihsan due to people's need for it, for the plaintiff may find it difficult to gather his witnesses and his opponent. So it resembles testimony upon testimony, and just as testimony upon testimony is permitted to revive the rights of the people.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on a judge sending written testimony to another judge (كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي or الكتاب الحكمي). The base text states that the judge writes the testimony so that the receiving judge can judge by it, and this is called the judgmental letter. It is accepted in matters that are not nullified by suspicion (i.e., not in hudud or qisas). The commentary explains that the writing judge does not issue a judgment himself; he merely transmits the testimony. The receiving judge judges according to his own opinion, even if it differs from the writing judge, unlike the record (السجل) which is a final judgment. Conditions are required: both judges must be known, the claim and parties must be known. Although analogy (qiyas) would reject this practice because if the writing judge personally appeared and testified orally, it would not be accepted (as he is not a witness), and there is risk of forgery, yet the scholars permitted it by istihsan (juristic preference) due to necessity. The need arises because a plaintiff may not be able to bring both his witnesses and his opponent to the distant court. This is similar to the permissibility of testifying upon testimony (الشهادة على الشهادة), which is allowed to protect people's rights.

Key Terms
الكتاب الحكمي (al-kitāb al-ḥukmī): A letter from one judge to another containing testimony, for the receiving judge to issue a judgment.
نقل الشهادة (naql al-shahādah): Transmission of testimony from one judge to another via letter.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to necessity, public interest, or equity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the judge's letter to another judge accepted despite the risk of forgery?
A) Because it is a stronger proof than oral testimony.
B) Because of necessity (حاجة) and it is analogous to testimony upon testimony.
C) Because the seal guarantees authenticity.
D) Because the writing judge is reliable.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the judge's letter (الكتاب الحكمي) by istihsan to protect rights, overriding qiyas, under conditions of known parties and excluding hudud/qisas.

The Permissibility of the Judge's Book: Between Qiyas and Istihsan
Explaining the permissibility, conditions, and scope of the judge's book by istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits the judge's book despite qiyas, identify its conditions, and determine its scope of application.

Core Idea
Istihsan permits the judge's book over qiyas, because people's need for testimony transfer outweighs the risk of forgery.

In this passage, the commentator expands on the ruling that a judge may write testimony to another judge, allowing the recipient to judge using his own reasoning. The text explains why qiyas would reject this practice but istihsan overrides it, drawing an analogy to testimony upon testimony. We will explore the conditions, the scope (excluding hudud and qisas), and the reasoning behind the inclusion of various claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
State the ruling: it is permissible (ja'iz) to act upon the judge's book. The primary proof is istihsan, supported by public need and the report of Ali (RA) and agreement of jurists.
The text says: 'جوز استحساناً لحاجة الناس إليه' (permitted by istihsan due to people's need).
2
Understand the qiyas objection
Explain why qiyas would prohibit the practice: the writing judge's oral testimony in person would not be accepted, and written documents carry suspicion of forgery.
The analogy (qiyas) is based on the asl: oral testimony of the writing judge in the recipient's court is not accepted.
3
Analyze the istihsan justification
The istihsan justification rests on two pillars: (1) widespread need – plaintiffs cannot always bring witnesses and opponent together; (2) analogy to testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala shahada), which is also permitted despite weakness.
The text says: 'فأشبه الشهادة على الشهادة' (so it resembles testimony upon testimony).
4
Determine the conditions
Identify the four conditions: the book must be from a known judge to a known judge, concerning a known claim, for a known claimant, against a known defendant.
The text: 'ويشترط في الكتاب على أن يكون من معلوم إلى معلوم، في مدعى به معلوم لمدع معلوم على مدعى عليه معلوم'.
5
Identify the scope and exclusions
Determine what is included: debts, real estate, marriage, lineage, stolen property, and denied trust/mudarabah. Excluded: hudud and qisas because they are dropped by doubt.
The text: 'يقبل فيما لا يسقط بشبهة' (accepted in what is not invalidated by a doubt).
6
Apply to specific examples
Work through the examples: debt is known by amount and description; real estate by boundary; marriage itself does not require pointing; lineage by mentioning ancestors; stolen property value becomes a debt.
The commentator addresses an objection about marriage requiring pointing and resolves it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكتب بالشهادة ليحكم المكتوب إليه بها، وهو الكتاب الحكمي، وكتاب القاضي إلى القاضي، وهو نقل الشهادة حقيقة، ويقبل فيما لا يسقط بشبهة. قوله: وكتب؛ القاضي بالشهادة إلى قاض يكون الخصم في ولايته؛ ليحكم القاضي المكتوب إليه على وجه الخصم؛ لئلا يكون قضاء على الغائب. قوله: وهو؛ أي ما كتب القاضي فيه الشهادة؛ ليحكم المكتوب إليه بها الكتاب الحكمي المنسوب إلى الحكم باعتبار ما يؤول إليه، أو كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي. ووجه التسمية به ظاهر، وهو نقل الشهادة حقيقة؛ لأن الكاتب لم يحكم بها، وإنما نقلها للمكتوب إليه ليحكم بها؛ ولهذا يحكم المكتوب إليه برأيه، وإن خالف رأيه رأي الكاتب بخلاف السجل كما مر آنفاً. ويشترط في الكتاب على أن يكون من معلوم إلى معلوم، في مدعى به معلوم لمدع معلوم على مدعى عليه معلوم، والقياس يأبى جواز العمل بكتاب القاضي إلى القاضي؛ لأن القاضي الكاتب لو حضر بنفسه مجلس المكتوب إليه وخبره بلسانه عما في الكتاب لا يعمل به القاضي، فكيف بالكتاب. وفيه شبهة التزوير، إذ الخط يشبه الخط، والخاتم يشبه الخاتم، إلا أنه جوز استحساناً؛ لحاجة الناس إليه، فإن المدعي قد يتعذر عليه الجمع بين شهوده وخصمه، فأشبه الشهادة على الشهادة، فكما جوز الشهادة على الشهادة؛ لإحياء حقوق العباد إذا شهد به عنده كالدين، والعقار، والنكاح، والنسب، والمغصوب، والأمانة والمضاربة المجحودتين، أي ما سوى الحدود والقصاص، إذا شهد به عنده كالدين، والعقار، والنكاح، والنسب، والمغصوب، والأمانة والمضاربة المجحودتين، فإن الأمانة، ومال المضاربة إذا لم يجحدا لا يحتاج إلى كتاب القاضي، وإذا جحدا صارا مغصوبين، وفي المغصوب تجب القيمة، وهي دين، فيجري فيه الكتاب الحكمي. قوله: أي ما سوى الحدود والقصاص؛ لأن مبناهما على الإسقاط بأدنى شبهة، وفي قبوله سعي في إثباتهما. قوله: كالدين؛ فإنه يعرف بالقدر والوصف، ولا يحتاج فيه إلى الإشارة. والعقار: فإنه أيضاً يعرف بالتحديد. والنكاح: سواء ادعى الزوج أو الزوجة. وكذلك الطلاق. فإن اختلج في قلبك أن الإشارة في باب النكاح شرط، وكتاب القاضي إلى القاضي فيما يحتاج إلى الإشارة غير جائز، فكيف يدخل النكاح تحت هذا الحكم، فأزحه بأن المدعى به نفس النكاح، وهو لا يحتاج إلى الإشارة، والإشارة إلى الخصم شرط، وهو الزوج أو الزوجة، وهو ليس بمدعى به، فصار النكاح نظير الدين في الذمة، والإشارة إلى الغريم شرط، ومع هذا جاز كتاب القاضي فيه، فكذا هاهنا. والنسب: سواء كان من قبل الحي أو الميت؛ لأنه يعرف بذكر الأب والجد. والمغصوب: إذ فيه يلزم القيمة، وهي دين.
And he wrote with the testimony so that the recipient judge may judge by it, and it is the 'book of judgment' (al-kitab al-hukmi), and the judge's book to the judge, which is the transfer of testimony in reality, and it is accepted in what is not invalidated by a doubt. His saying: 'And he wrote': the judge writes with the testimony to a judge in whose jurisdiction the opponent is, so that the recipient judge may judge against the opponent, lest it be a judgment against the absent. His saying: 'And it is': i.e., what the judge wrote the testimony in, for the recipient judge to judge by it, is the 'book of judgment' attributed to judgment by virtue of what it leads to, or the judge's book to the judge. The reason for this naming is apparent: it is the transfer of testimony in reality, because the writer did not judge by it, but rather transferred it to the recipient to judge by it; hence the recipient judges according to his own opinion, even if it contradicts the opinion of the writer, unlike the court record (sijill) as previously mentioned. Conditions for the book: it must be from a known (judge) to a known (judge), concerning a known claim, for a known claimant, against a known defendant. Analogy (qiyas) opposes the permissibility of acting upon the judge's book to the judge, because if the writing judge himself had attended the recipient's court and informed him orally of what is in the book, the judge would not act upon it, so how much less through writing? And there is the suspicion of forgery, since handwriting resembles handwriting, and seals resemble seals. However, it has been permitted by istihsan (juristic preference) due to people's need, because for the plaintiff it may be difficult to gather his witnesses and his opponent together, so it resembles testimony upon testimony. Just as testimony upon testimony is permitted to revive the rights of people (al-ibad), when it is testified before him, such as debt, real estate, marriage, lineage, stolen property, and the denied trust and mudarabah—meaning anything except hudud and qisas, when it is testified before him, like debt, real estate, marriage, lineage, stolen property, and the denied trust and mudarabah. For the trust and mudarabah property, if they are not denied, there is no need for the judge's book; but if they are denied, they become like stolen property, and in stolen property the value is obligatory—it is a debt—so the book of judgment applies therein. His saying: 'meaning anything except hudud and qisas' because they are based on dropping (the penalty) at the slightest doubt, and accepting it (the book) would be striving to establish them. His saying: 'like debt' because it is known by amount and description, and there is no need for pointing (to the subject matter). Real estate: also known by boundary marking. Marriage: whether claimed by the husband or wife; likewise divorce. If it occurs to your mind that pointing is a condition in the chapter of marriage, and the judge's book in matters requiring pointing is not permissible, so how does marriage come under this ruling? Remove this doubt by saying: the claimed matter is the marriage itself, which does not require pointing; pointing to the opponent is a condition, and the opponent is the husband or wife, who is not the claimed matter; thus marriage is analogous to a debt in the liability (dhimmah), where pointing to the debtor is a condition, yet the judge's book is permitted therein—so here too. Lineage: whether from the living or the dead, because it is known by mentioning the father and grandfather. Stolen property: because therein the value is obligatory, and it is a debt.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the ruling regarding the judge's book (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi). It begins by distinguishing between two types of writing: the 'book of judgment' (al-kitab al-hukmi) which is a letter from a judge to another containing testimony so that the recipient may judge by it, and the 'judge's book' proper, which is the actual transfer of testimony. The key difference from a court record (sijill) is that the recipient judge may use his own independent reasoning (ra'y), even if it contradicts the writer's opinion, whereas in a sijill the judgment is binding and cannot be overruled. The commentator then lists the conditions: the book must be from and to known judges, with a known claim, claimant, and defendant. He acknowledges that qiyas (analogy) would reject such a practice because oral testimony from the writing judge in person would not be accepted, and written documents are susceptible to forgery. However, by istihsan (juristic preference), it is permitted due to public need: plaintiffs often cannot bring their witnesses and opponent together. It is compared to testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala shahada), which is also permitted for reviving people's rights. The scope of acceptance is limited to matters that are not invalidated by a doubt (i.e., civil rights and financial transactions), excluding hudud and qisas because these penalties are dropped by the slightest doubt, and the book would be an effort to establish them. Examples are given: debts, real estate, marriage, lineage, stolen property, and denied trust/mudarabah. The commentator addresses an objection regarding marriage: pointing (ishara) to the subject matter is not necessary because the claimed matter is the marriage itself, not the spouse, just as in debt the pointing is to the debtor, not the debt. Similarly, lineage is known by mentioning ancestors. Stolen property is included because the value (qimah) becomes a debt.

Key Terms
الكتاب الحكمي (al-kitab al-hukmi): A letter from a judge to another judge containing testimony, intended for the recipient to judge by it, named for its eventual outcome (judgment).
نقل الشهادة (naql al-shahada): Transfer of testimony; the writing judge transmits the witnesses' testimony to the recipient judge without himself judging.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; abandoning the ruling of qiyas for a stronger ruling due to need, public interest, or equity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school permit the judge's book (kitab al-qadi) despite qiyas opposing it?
A) Because it is explicitly commanded in the Quran
B) Because of istihsan due to public need and analogy to testimony upon testimony
C) Because the writing judge's testimony is considered more reliable
D) Because it is required by ijma' of all scholars

Key Takeaway
The judge's book is a permissible transfer of testimony by istihsan, overriding qiyas, and is accepted in civil matters but not in hudud and qisas.

Qada — Judiciary

Conditions and Scope of the Judge's Letter
Explains validity conditions and scope of judge's letter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for a valid judge's letter and identify which types of claims are accepted under Hanafi law.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is valid only when five parties are known and the claim is knowable by description, not requiring physical pointing.

The Hanafi school permits judges to communicate claims via letter, but strict conditions apply. This lesson explains the five essential conditions (al-‘ulum al-khams) and the types of claims that qualify, such as debt, real estate, marriage, and lineage. It also clarifies why hudud, qisas, and movable property are excluded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five known elements
List the five conditions: the writing judge must be known, the receiving judge known, the subject matter known, the plaintiff known, and the defendant known. These are called 'al-‘ulum al-khams'.
2
Recognize accepted claims
Identify claims that do not require physical reference (ishara): debt (knowable by amount/description), real estate (boundaries), marriage (the contract itself), lineage (ancestors), usurped property (value becomes debt), denied trust and mudarabah, preemption, agency, will, death, inheritance, and homicide with monetary penalty.
These are known by amount, description, or both.
3
Exclude hudud and qisas
Understand that hudud and qisas are excluded because they are built on dropping at the slightest doubt; accepting a letter would be striving to establish them.
4
Understand the rationale against movable property
Note that movable property (e.g., garments, slaves) requires physical pointing (ishara) in claim and testimony, so a judge's letter is not accepted – a key distinction that leads to an internal dispute.

إذا شُهِدَ به عنده كالدين، والعقار، والنكاح ، والنَّسب، والمغصوب، والأمانة والمضاربة المجحودتين أي ما سوى الحدود والقصاص ، إذا شُهِدَ به عنده كالدين، والعقار، والنكاح، والنسب، والمغصوب، والأمانة والمضاربة المجحودتين)، فإنَّ الأمانة ، ومال المضاربة إذا لم يُجحدا لا يُحتاجُ إلى كتاب القاضي، وإذا جُجدا صارا مغصوبين، وفي المغصوب تجب القيمة، وهي دين، فيجري فيه الكتاب الحكمي، إذ لا احتياج إلى الإشارة كذلك ، جوز الكتاب لذلك. فإن قلت : لا حاجة إليه إذ يستغنى عنه بالشهادة على الشهادة. قلت : القاضي يحتاج في الشهادةِ على الشهادة إلى تعديل الأصول، وقد يتعدَّرُ ذلك في تلك البلدة، فتقعُ الحاجة إلى نقل شهادتهم بالكتاب، وأيضاً قد يتعسر نقل الشهادةِ إذ أكثر الناس لا يحسن ذلك، بخلاف كتاب القاضي فإنّه تُعَدَّلُ فيه الشهود، ولا يحتاج فيه إلى نقل الشهادة ، ورُوِيَ أَنَّ عليّا الله جوزه لذلك، وعليه أجمع الفقهاء. ١ ] قوله : أي ما سوى الحدود والقصاص ؛ لأنَّ مبناهما على الإسقاط بأدنى شبهة، وفي قبوله سعي في إثباتهما. (۲) قوله : كالدين ؛ فإنّه يعرفُ بالقدر والوصف، ولا يحتاج فيه إلى الإشارة. والعقار: فإنّه أيضاً يعرف بالتحديد. والنكاحُ : سواء ادّعى الزوج أو الزوجة. وكذلك الطلاق. فإن اختلج في قلبك أنّ الإشارة في باب النكاح شرط، وكتاب القاضي إلى القاضي فيما يحتاج إلى الإشارة غير جائز ، فكيف يدخلُ النّكاحُ تحت هذا الحكم، فأزحه بأن المدعى به نفس النكاح ، وهو لا يحتاج إلى الإشارة، والإشارة إلى الخصم شرط ، وهو الزوج أو الزوجة، وهو ليس بمدعی به ، فصار النكاح نظير الدين في الذمة، والإشارة إلى الغريم شرط، ومع هذا جاز كتاب القاضي فيه، فكذا هاهنا. والنسب: سواء كان من قبل الحي أو الميت ؛ لأنه يعرفُ بذكر الأب والجد. والمغصوب : إذ فيه يلزم القيمة، وهي دين. بل يعرفُ بالصفةِ بخلاف العين المنقولة ، فإِنَّهُ يَحْتاجُ فيها إلى الإشارة، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له ، وكذا عند أبي يوسف له إلا في العبد الآبق فيقبلُ فيه. وقد ذكر في كيفيّتِهِ هكذا : يكتب قاضي بُخارا إلى قاضي سَمَرْقَنْدَ : إِنَّ فلاناً وفلاناً شهدا عندي أن عبد فلان المسمّى بالمبارك الذي حليته كذا وكذا، أيق من مالكه ووقع بسمرقند في يد فلان إلى آخر الكتاب والأمانة والمضاربة المجحودتين؛ لأنهما كالمغصوب حكماً، قيدهما بالمجحودتين لتكونا بمنزلة الدين ، إذ لو لم تكن الأمانة أو المضاربة مجحودة لكانت من جملة الأعيان المنقولة، فلا يقبلُ كتاب القاضي فيها، وكذا الشفعة والوكالة والوصية والوفاة والوراثة، والقتل الذي يوجب المال ؛ لأنَّ البعض منها يعرف بالقدر والوصف والبعض الآخر يعرف بأحدهما. ١ ] قوله : بخلاف العين المنقولة ؛ كالثوب والعبدِ والأمة ونحوها، فإنّ فيها لا يقبلُ كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي ؛ فإنّه يحتاج فيها إلى الإشارة عند الدعوى والشهادة، وفيما يحتاج فيه إلى الإشارة لا يقبل. وهذا أي عدم القبول عند أبي حنيفة له ، وهو ظاهر الرواية، وكذا لا يقبلُ فيها عند أبي يوسف له إلا في العبد الآبق فيقبل فيه ؛ لأنَّ الإباق يغلب فيه لا في الأمة، فإن العبد يخدم خارج البيت غالباً، فيقدر على الإباق، فيحسن الحاجة إلى الكتاب، بخلاف الأمة، فإنها داخل البيت غالباً، وعنه نه أيضاً أن يقبل في الأمة كالعبد. كما ذكروا. [٢) قوله : يكتب قاضي بخارا...الخ ؛ العلوم الخمسة شرط جواز كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي، وهو أن يكون الكتاب : ١. من معلوم : وهو القاضي الكاتب. ٢. إلى معلوم : وهو القاضي المكتوب إليه. ٣. في معلوم : وهو المدعى به. ٤. لمعلوم : وهو المدعي. ٥. على معلوم: وهو المدعى عليه.
If it is testified about before him, like debt, real estate, marriage, lineage, usurped property, trust property (amanah) and mudarabah when denied—i.e., other than hudud and qisas, if it is testified about before him, like debt, real estate, marriage, lineage, usurped property, and trust property and mudarabah when denied. Indeed, amanah and mudarabah capital if not denied do not require a judge's letter; if denied they become like usurped property, and in usurped property value is obligatory, and it is a debt, so the legal letter applies, since there is no need for physical reference. Likewise, the letter is permitted for that. If you say: there is no need because it can be substituted by testimony upon testimony. I say: the judge in testimony upon testimony needs verification of the original witnesses, and that may be difficult in that town, so the need arises to transmit their testimony by letter. Also, transferring testimony may be difficult because most people do not do it well, unlike the judge's letter wherein the witnesses are verified, and there is no need to transfer testimony. It is narrated that Ali, may God be pleased with him, permitted it for that reason, and the jurists have consensus upon it. [1] His statement: i.e., other than hudud and qisas because they are based on dropping at the slightest doubt, and accepting them is an effort to establish them. (2) His statement: like debt; it is known by amount and description, and does not require physical reference. Real estate: it is also known by boundaries. Marriage: whether the husband or wife claims. Similarly divorce. If it occurs to you that physical reference in marriage is a condition, and a judge's letter to another judge regarding what requires physical reference is not permissible, so how is marriage included under this ruling? Remove it by [saying] that what is claimed is the marriage itself, which does not require physical reference, and physical reference to the opponent is a condition, and he is the husband or wife, and he is not the object claimed. So marriage becomes analogous to a debt in the dhimmah, and physical reference to the debtor is a condition, yet the judge's letter is permitted therein, so here too. Lineage: whether from the living or the dead, because it is known by mentioning the father and grandfather. Usurped property: because therein value is obligatory, and it is a debt. Rather it is known by description unlike movable property, for it requires physical reference. This according to Abu Hanifa, may God have mercy on him, and similarly according to Abu Yusuf, may God have mercy on him, except in the case of a runaway slave, then it is accepted. It has been mentioned in its manner thus: The judge of Bukhara writes to the judge of Samarkand: So-and-so and so-and-so testified before me that the slave of so-and-so named al-Mubarak, whose description is such and such, escaped from his owner and ended up in Samarkand in the possession of so-and-so, etc. to the end of the letter. And trust property and mudarabah when denied, because they are like usurped property in legal effect. He qualified them with 'when denied' so that they become akin to debt, because if the trust property or mudarabah were not denied, they would be among movable objects, so the judge's letter would not be accepted therein. Likewise preemption, agency, will, death, inheritance, and homicide that necessitates wealth, because some of them are known by amount and description and some by one of them. [1] His statement: unlike movable property, like a garment, slave, slave-girl, and similar, for therein the judge's letter to another judge is not accepted, because it requires physical reference in claim and testimony, and what requires physical reference is not accepted. This, i.e., non-acceptance, according to Abu Hanifa, may God have mercy on him, and it is the apparent narration, and likewise it is not accepted according to Abu Yusuf, may God have mercy on him, except in the case of a runaway slave, it is accepted because running away is prevalent in him, not in a slave-girl, for the male slave serves outside the house usually, so he can run away, so the need for the letter is appropriate, unlike the female slave, for she is inside the house usually. It is also narrated from him that he accepts in the case of a slave-girl like the male slave, as they mentioned. [2] His statement: The judge of Bukhara writes... etc. The five known elements are conditions for the validity of a judge's letter to another judge, that the letter be: 1. From a known entity: the writing judge. 2. To a known entity: the receiving judge. 3. Regarding a known entity: the subject of claim. 4. For a known entity: the plaintiff. 5. Against a known entity: the defendant.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the ruling concerning the judge's letter (kitab al-qadi) to another judge. The author explains that a judge's letter is accepted for claims where the subject matter is known by description or amount without needing physical reference (ishara). These include debts (knowable by amount and description), real estate (knowable by boundaries), marriage (the claim itself does not require ishara, though pointing to the spouse is a condition for procedure), lineage (knowable by mentioning ancestors), and usurped property (since the value is owed as a debt). Trust property and mudarabah capital are included only when denied, because then they become like debts. The letter is also accepted for preemption, agency, will, death, inheritance, and homicide that entails monetary compensation. The legal reasoning is that these matters are either known by amount and description or by one of them.

The commentator then addresses a potential objection: why not simply use testimony upon testimony (shahada ‘ala shahada)? The response is that testimony upon testimony requires verification of original witnesses, which may be difficult in a distant town, and transferring testimony is not easy for most people. A judge's letter, however, has the witnesses verified and avoids the need for direct transfer. This is supported by a narration from ‘Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and consensus of jurists.

Crucially, the passage distinguishes movable property (al-‘ayn al-manqula) such as garments, slaves, and slave-girls. According to Abu Hanifa, a judge's letter is not accepted for movable property because they require ishara (physical pointing) during claim and testimony. Abu Yusuf agrees except in the case of a runaway slave (‘abd abiq), because a male slave often works outside and can run away, creating a practical need for the letter. There is also a narration from Abu Yusuf accepting it for a female slave as well.

Finally, the commentator lists five conditions for the validity of a judge's letter: the writer (judge) must be known, the recipient (judge) must be known, the subject matter must be known, the plaintiff must be known, and the defendant must be known. These are summarized as 'al-‘ulum al-khams' (the five known elements).

Key Terms
كتاب القاضي (kitab al-qadi): A written communication from one judge to another judge regarding a legal claim or evidence.
الإشارة (al-ishara): Physical pointing or identification of an object in court proceedings.
العلوم الخمسة (al-‘ulum al-khams): The five known elements that are conditions for a judge's letter: writer, recipient, subject, plaintiff, defendant all must be known.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the five conditions for a valid judge's letter?
A) The writing judge is known.
B) The witnesses are present in the letter.
C) The subject matter is known.
D) The defendant is known.

Key Takeaway
The five known elements are essential for a judge's letter to be valid; only claims knowable by description (not requiring ishara) qualify, with exceptions for hudud, qisas, and movable property.

Qada — Judiciary

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Movable Property in Judge's Letters
Details intra-Hanafi dispute on movable property in judge's letters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the acceptance of a judge's letter for movable property, and state the exception for a runaway slave.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa rejects judge's letters for movable property because they require ishara; Abu Yusuf makes an exception for runaway slaves due to practical necessity.

While most claims are accepted via judge's letter, movable property presents a problem because it requires physical pointing (ishara). This lesson focuses on the internal Hanafi disagreement: Abu Hanifa's absolute rejection versus Abu Yusuf's limited exception for the runaway slave, and the reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Movable property (al-‘ayn al-manqula) such as garments, slaves, and slave-girls requires physical pointing (ishara) in claim and testimony; therefore, a judge's letter is not accepted.
This is the default position (zahir al-riwayah).
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that no movable property is accepted via letter, without exception. This is the apparent transmission.
3
Identify Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifa except for a runaway male slave (al-‘abd al-abiq); he accepts a letter for such a slave. There is also a narration from him accepting for a female slave as well.
4
Understand the illa (effective cause)
For the runaway slave, running away is prevalent because male slaves often work outside the home, so there is a practical need for the letter. The slave can be identified by description, reducing the need for ishara.
Female slaves usually stay inside, so running away is less common; hence, Abu Yusuf's preferred view does not extend to them.
5
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a judge cannot send a letter about a stolen garment, but can send one about a runaway male slave according to Abu Yusuf. Abu Hanifa would reject both.

Source Text

إذا شُهِدَ به عنده كالدين، والعقار، والنكاح ، والنَّسب، والمغصوب، والأمانة والمضاربة المجحودتين أي ما سوى الحدود والقصاص ، إذا شُهِدَ به عنده كالدين، والعقار، والنكاح، والنسب، والمغصوب، والأمانة والمضاربة المجحودتين)، فإنَّ الأمانة ، ومال المضاربة إذا لم يُجحدا لا يُحتاجُ إلى كتاب القاضي، وإذا جُجدا صارا مغصوبين، وفي المغصوب تجب القيمة، وهي دين، فيجري فيه الكتاب الحكمي، إذ لا احتياج إلى الإشارة كذلك ، جوز الكتاب لذلك. فإن قلت : لا حاجة إليه إذ يستغنى عنه بالشهادة على الشهادة. قلت : القاضي يحتاج في الشهادةِ على الشهادة إلى تعديل الأصول، وقد يتعدَّرُ ذلك في تلك البلدة، فتقعُ الحاجة إلى نقل شهادتهم بالكتاب، وأيضاً قد يتعسر نقل الشهادةِ إذ أكثر الناس لا يحسن ذلك، بخلاف كتاب القاضي فإنّه تُعَدَّلُ فيه الشهود، ولا يحتاج فيه إلى نقل الشهادة ، ورُوِيَ أَنَّ عليّا الله جوزه لذلك، وعليه أجمع الفقهاء. ١ ] قوله : أي ما سوى الحدود والقصاص ؛ لأنَّ مبناهما على الإسقاط بأدنى شبهة، وفي قبوله سعي في إثباتهما. (۲) قوله : كالدين ؛ فإنّه يعرفُ بالقدر والوصف، ولا يحتاج فيه إلى الإشارة. والعقار: فإنّه أيضاً يعرف بالتحديد. والنكاحُ : سواء ادّعى الزوج أو الزوجة. وكذلك الطلاق. فإن اختلج في قلبك أنّ الإشارة في باب النكاح شرط، وكتاب القاضي إلى القاضي فيما يحتاج إلى الإشارة غير جائز ، فكيف يدخلُ النّكاحُ تحت هذا الحكم، فأزحه بأن المدعى به نفس النكاح ، وهو لا يحتاج إلى الإشارة، والإشارة إلى الخصم شرط ، وهو الزوج أو الزوجة، وهو ليس بمدعی به ، فصار النكاح نظير الدين في الذمة، والإشارة إلى الغريم شرط، ومع هذا جاز كتاب القاضي فيه، فكذا هاهنا. والنسب: سواء كان من قبل الحي أو الميت ؛ لأنه يعرفُ بذكر الأب والجد. والمغصوب : إذ فيه يلزم القيمة، وهي دين. بل يعرفُ بالصفةِ بخلاف العين المنقولة ، فإِنَّهُ يَحْتاجُ فيها إلى الإشارة، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له ، وكذا عند أبي يوسف له إلا في العبد الآبق فيقبلُ فيه. وقد ذكر في كيفيّتِهِ هكذا : يكتب قاضي بُخارا إلى قاضي سَمَرْقَنْدَ : إِنَّ فلاناً وفلاناً شهدا عندي أن عبد فلان المسمّى بالمبارك الذي حليته كذا وكذا، أيق من مالكه ووقع بسمرقند في يد فلان إلى آخر الكتاب والأمانة والمضاربة المجحودتين؛ لأنهما كالمغصوب حكماً، قيدهما بالمجحودتين لتكونا بمنزلة الدين ، إذ لو لم تكن الأمانة أو المضاربة مجحودة لكانت من جملة الأعيان المنقولة، فلا يقبلُ كتاب القاضي فيها، وكذا الشفعة والوكالة والوصية والوفاة والوراثة، والقتل الذي يوجب المال ؛ لأنَّ البعض منها يعرف بالقدر والوصف والبعض الآخر يعرف بأحدهما. ١ ] قوله : بخلاف العين المنقولة ؛ كالثوب والعبدِ والأمة ونحوها، فإنّ فيها لا يقبلُ كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي ؛ فإنّه يحتاج فيها إلى الإشارة عند الدعوى والشهادة، وفيما يحتاج فيه إلى الإشارة لا يقبل. وهذا أي عدم القبول عند أبي حنيفة له ، وهو ظاهر الرواية، وكذا لا يقبلُ فيها عند أبي يوسف له إلا في العبد الآبق فيقبل فيه ؛ لأنَّ الإباق يغلب فيه لا في الأمة، فإن العبد يخدم خارج البيت غالباً، فيقدر على الإباق، فيحسن الحاجة إلى الكتاب، بخلاف الأمة، فإنها داخل البيت غالباً، وعنه نه أيضاً أن يقبل في الأمة كالعبد. كما ذكروا. [٢) قوله : يكتب قاضي بخارا...الخ ؛ العلوم الخمسة شرط جواز كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي، وهو أن يكون الكتاب : ١. من معلوم : وهو القاضي الكاتب. ٢. إلى معلوم : وهو القاضي المكتوب إليه. ٣. في معلوم : وهو المدعى به. ٤. لمعلوم : وهو المدعي. ٥. على معلوم: وهو المدعى عليه.
If it is testified about before him, like debt, real estate, marriage, lineage, usurped property, trust property (amanah) and mudarabah when denied—i.e., other than hudud and qisas, if it is testified about before him, like debt, real estate, marriage, lineage, usurped property, and trust property and mudarabah when denied. Indeed, amanah and mudarabah capital if not denied do not require a judge's letter; if denied they become like usurped property, and in usurped property value is obligatory, and it is a debt, so the legal letter applies, since there is no need for physical reference. Likewise, the letter is permitted for that. If you say: there is no need because it can be substituted by testimony upon testimony. I say: the judge in testimony upon testimony needs verification of the original witnesses, and that may be difficult in that town, so the need arises to transmit their testimony by letter. Also, transferring testimony may be difficult because most people do not do it well, unlike the judge's letter wherein the witnesses are verified, and there is no need to transfer testimony. It is narrated that Ali, may God be pleased with him, permitted it for that reason, and the jurists have consensus upon it. [1] His statement: i.e., other than hudud and qisas because they are based on dropping at the slightest doubt, and accepting them is an effort to establish them. (2) His statement: like debt; it is known by amount and description, and does not require physical reference. Real estate: it is also known by boundaries. Marriage: whether the husband or wife claims. Similarly divorce. If it occurs to you that physical reference in marriage is a condition, and a judge's letter to another judge regarding what requires physical reference is not permissible, so how is marriage included under this ruling? Remove it by [saying] that what is claimed is the marriage itself, which does not require physical reference, and physical reference to the opponent is a condition, and he is the husband or wife, and he is not the object claimed. So marriage becomes analogous to a debt in the dhimmah, and physical reference to the debtor is a condition, yet the judge's letter is permitted therein, so here too. Lineage: whether from the living or the dead, because it is known by mentioning the father and grandfather. Usurped property: because therein value is obligatory, and it is a debt. Rather it is known by description unlike movable property, for it requires physical reference. This according to Abu Hanifa, may God have mercy on him, and similarly according to Abu Yusuf, may God have mercy on him, except in the case of a runaway slave, then it is accepted. It has been mentioned in its manner thus: The judge of Bukhara writes to the judge of Samarkand: So-and-so and so-and-so testified before me that the slave of so-and-so named al-Mubarak, whose description is such and such, escaped from his owner and ended up in Samarkand in the possession of so-and-so, etc. to the end of the letter. And trust property and mudarabah when denied, because they are like usurped property in legal effect. He qualified them with 'when denied' so that they become akin to debt, because if the trust property or mudarabah were not denied, they would be among movable objects, so the judge's letter would not be accepted therein. Likewise preemption, agency, will, death, inheritance, and homicide that necessitates wealth, because some of them are known by amount and description and some by one of them. [1] His statement: unlike movable property, like a garment, slave, slave-girl, and similar, for therein the judge's letter to another judge is not accepted, because it requires physical reference in claim and testimony, and what requires physical reference is not accepted. This, i.e., non-acceptance, according to Abu Hanifa, may God have mercy on him, and it is the apparent narration, and likewise it is not accepted according to Abu Yusuf, may God have mercy on him, except in the case of a runaway slave, it is accepted because running away is prevalent in him, not in a slave-girl, for the male slave serves outside the house usually, so he can run away, so the need for the letter is appropriate, unlike the female slave, for she is inside the house usually. It is also narrated from him that he accepts in the case of a slave-girl like the male slave, as they mentioned. [2] His statement: The judge of Bukhara writes... etc. The five known elements are conditions for the validity of a judge's letter to another judge, that the letter be: 1. From a known entity: the writing judge. 2. To a known entity: the receiving judge. 3. Regarding a known entity: the subject of claim. 4. For a known entity: the plaintiff. 5. Against a known entity: the defendant.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the ruling concerning the judge's letter (kitab al-qadi) to another judge. The author explains that a judge's letter is accepted for claims where the subject matter is known by description or amount without needing physical reference (ishara). These include debts (knowable by amount and description), real estate (knowable by boundaries), marriage (the claim itself does not require ishara, though pointing to the spouse is a condition for procedure), lineage (knowable by mentioning ancestors), and usurped property (since the value is owed as a debt). Trust property and mudarabah capital are included only when denied, because then they become like debts. The letter is also accepted for preemption, agency, will, death, inheritance, and homicide that entails monetary compensation. The legal reasoning is that these matters are either known by amount and description or by one of them.

The commentator then addresses a potential objection: why not simply use testimony upon testimony (shahada ‘ala shahada)? The response is that testimony upon testimony requires verification of original witnesses, which may be difficult in a distant town, and transferring testimony is not easy for most people. A judge's letter, however, has the witnesses verified and avoids the need for direct transfer. This is supported by a narration from ‘Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and consensus of jurists.

Crucially, the passage distinguishes movable property (al-‘ayn al-manqula) such as garments, slaves, and slave-girls. According to Abu Hanifa, a judge's letter is not accepted for movable property because they require ishara (physical pointing) during claim and testimony. Abu Yusuf agrees except in the case of a runaway slave (‘abd abiq), because a male slave often works outside and can run away, creating a practical need for the letter. There is also a narration from Abu Yusuf accepting it for a female slave as well.

Finally, the commentator lists five conditions for the validity of a judge's letter: the writer (judge) must be known, the recipient (judge) must be known, the subject matter must be known, the plaintiff must be known, and the defendant must be known. These are summarized as 'al-‘ulum al-khams' (the five known elements).

Key Terms
العين المنقولة (al-ayn al-manqula): Movable property (e.g., garments, slaves) that requires physical identification.
العبد الآبق (al-abd al-abiq): A male slave who has run away from his owner.
الإشارة (al-ishara): Physical pointing or identification of an object in court proceedings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a judge's letter concerning a runaway slave (عبد آبق) according to Abu Yusuf?
A) It is accepted by both Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
B) It is not accepted by either Abu Hanifa or Abu Yusuf.
C) It is accepted only by Abu Yusuf, not by Abu Hanifa.
D) It is accepted only by Abu Hanifa, not by Abu Yusuf.

Key Takeaway
The general rule that movable property is not accepted via judge's letter is modified only for a runaway male slave (and possibly female) according to Abu Yusuf, but Abu Hanifa's stricter view remains the relied-upon position.

The Judge's Letter: Movable vs Immovable Property and the Runaway Slave Exception
Ruling on movable vs immovable property and exception for runaway slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on accepting a judge's letter for movable property and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the runaway slave.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is not accepted for movable property because it requires physical pointing; Abu Yusuf excepts the runaway slave due to his frequent absence.

This lesson examines a specific procedural rule in Hanafi qada: when a judge's letter (kitab al-qadi) can be used as evidence. The source distinguishes between immovable property (known by description) and movable property (requires physical indication). We will focus on the ruling for movable property and the notable intra-Hanafi difference regarding a runaway slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the distinction
Distinguish between immovable property (known by description, letter accepted) and movable property (requires pointing, letter not accepted).
Immovable like land; movable like a garment or slave.
2
State the general rule
For movable property, the judge's letter is not accepted because the claimant and witnesses must physically point to the object (isharah) in court.
This is the rule according to both Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that the letter is never accepted for any movable property, including a runaway slave. Abu Yusuf makes an exception for a runaway slave.
There is also a narration that Abu Yusuf accepts for a slave-girl as well.
4
Understand the reasoning
Abu Yusuf reasons that a runaway slave is often outside the house, making pointing impractical; the need for a letter is greater. For a slave-girl, she is usually inside, so the exception is less justified.
The text mentions that the slave serves outside mostly, hence the exception.

Source Text

والأمانة والمضاربة المجحودتين؛ لأنهما كالمغصوب حكماً، قيدهما بالمجحودتين لتكونا بمنزلة الدين ، إذ لو لم تكن الأمانة أو المضاربة مجحودة لكانت من جملة الأعيان المنقولة، فلا يقبلُ كتاب القاضي فيها، وكذا الشفعة والوكالة والوصية والوفاة والوراثة، والقتل الذي يوجب المال ؛ لأنَّ البعض منها يعرف بالقدر والوصف والبعض الآخر يعرف بأحدهما.
